style="font-size:91%;width:6em;top:6px;left:-3em"><div>WAW</div></div></div></div><div style="padding-top:0.2em">Location of airport in Poland</div></div></div></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black"><a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway"><span style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color:black;">Runways</span></a>\n</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data">\n<table style="width:100%; margin:-2px -1px -1px -1px; border-spacing:0;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="background-color: #e6e6ff">\n<th rowspan="2" style="width: 15%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; border-width:0 1px 0 0; text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/Runway#Naming" title="Runway">Direction</a>\n</th>\n<th colspan="2" style="width: 50%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; style="background-color: #e6e6ff">\n<th style="width: 20%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; border-width:1px 1px 0 1px; text-align: center;">m\n</th>\n<th style="width: 20%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; border-width:1px 1px 0 1px; text-align: center;">ft\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align: center;">11/29\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">2,800\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">9,186\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">Asphalt</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align: center;">15/33\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">3,690\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">12,106\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">Asphalt\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n</tbody></table></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black">Statistics (2019)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Passengers</th><td class="infobox-data">18,860,000</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Passenger change</th><td class="infobox-data"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />6.2%</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source: Passenger Traffic, ACI Europe<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Warsaw Chopin Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">Lotnisko Chopina w Warszawie</i>, <small>Polish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Polish" title="Help:IPA/Polish">[l\xc9\x94t\xcb\x88\xc9\xb2isk\xc9\x94 \xca\x82\xc9\x94p\xc9\x9bna]</a></span>) (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>WAW</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EPWA</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in the <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82ochy" title="W\xc5\x82ochy">W\xc5\x82ochy</a> district of <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>. It is Poland\'s <a href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_Europe_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Busiest airports in Europe by passenger traffic">busiest airport</a> with 18.9&#160;million passengers in 2019, thus handling approximately 40% of the country\'s total air passenger traffic. The airport is a central hub for <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a> as well as a base for <a href="/wiki/Nordica_(airline)" title="Nordica (airline)">Nordica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a>. \n</p><p>Warsaw Chopin Airport covers 834 hectares (2,060 acres) of land and handles approximately 300 scheduled flights daily, including a substantial number of charters. <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> are the busiest international connections, while <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Krak\xc3\xb3w">Krak\xc3\xb3w</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wroc\xc5\x82aw">Wroc\xc5\x82aw</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gda\xc5\x84sk">Gda\xc5\x84sk</a> are the most popular domestic ones.<sup id="cite_ref-tur-info_polish_source_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tur-info_polish_source-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Founded in 1934, the airport was previously known as <b>Warsaw-Okecie Airport</b> (<i lang="pl" title="Polish-language text">Port lotniczy Warszawa-Ok\xc4\x99cie</i>) and bore the name of its <a href="/wiki/Ok%C4%99cie" title="Ok\xc4\x99cie">Ok\xc4\x99cie</a> neighborhood throughout its history. It was renamed in honour of Polish composer and former Warsaw resident <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric Chopin">Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric Chopin</a> in 2001. Despite the official change, "Okecie" <i>(<i lang="pl" title="Polish-language text">"Lotnisko Ok\xc4\x99cie"</i>)</i> remains in popular and industry use, including air traffic and aerodrome references.\n</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport_railway_station" title="Warsaw Chopin Airport railway station">underground railway station</a> connected from the airport to Warsaw\'s suburban rail system was opened in June 2012 in time for the <a href="/wiki/Euro_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a> football championships, and on 25 November 2013, the airport announced accommodating \xe2\x80\x93 for the first time in history \xe2\x80\x93 its 10&#160;millionth passenger in a single year.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> A new and modern terminal was completed in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The secondary international airport of the city is the much smaller <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Modlin_Airport" title="Warsaw Modlin Airport">Warsaw Modlin Airport</a>, which opened in 2012 and is used for low-cost traffic.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span id="The_pre-war_and_wartime_Ok.C4.99cie_.281934.E2.80.9345.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_pre-war_and_wartime_Ok\xc4\x99cie_(1934\xe2\x80\x9345)">The pre-war and wartime Ok\xc4\x99cie (1934\xe2\x80\x9345)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The pre-war and wartime Ok\xc4\x99cie (1934\xe2\x80\x9345)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1924, when urban development around Warsaw\'s <a href="/wiki/Aerodrome" title="Aerodrome">aerodrome</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mokot%C3%B3w_Field" title="Mokot\xc3\xb3w Field">Mokot\xc3\xb3w Field</a> (Pole Mokotowskie) began affecting air traffic, the Ministry of Railways purchased land near the village of <a href="/wiki/Ok%C4%99cie" title="Ok\xc4\x99cie">Ok\xc4\x99cie</a> to construct a new airport. On 29 April 1934, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the Republic of Poland">Polish president</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ignacy_Mo%C5%9Bcicki" title="Ignacy Mo\xc5\x9bcicki">Ignacy Mo\xc5\x9bcicki</a>, opened Central Airport (Ok\xc4\x99cie), which from then on took over the handling of all traffic from the former civilian aerodrome at Pole Mokotowskie.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In the weeks after its opening, a journalist from the magazine <i>Flight and Air Defence of Poland</i> reported the following: "In a large pastel-coloured hall, we see a ticket office, a customs post, telegraph and post office, police station and a kiosk with various newspapers etc... On the first (upper) floor, there is a restaurant and viewing terrace, from where one can see the entire territory of the airport."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ok%C4%99cie_LOT_i_BA_1939.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ok%C4%99cie_LOT_i_BA_1939.jpeg/220px-Ok%C4%99cie_LOT_i_BA_1939.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ok%C4%99cie_LOT_i_BA_1939.jpeg/330px-Ok%C4%99cie_LOT_i_BA_1939.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ok%C4%99cie_LOT_i_BA_1939.jpeg/440px-Ok%C4%99cie_LOT_i_BA_1939.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ok%C4%99cie_LOT_i_BA_1939.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="British Airways Ltd.">British Airways</a> flight from Warsaw to London waits alongside a LOT <a href="/wiki/Junkers_Ju_52" title="Junkers Ju 52">Junkers Ju 52</a> at Ok\xc4\x99cie in April 1939</div></div></div>\n<p>With the building finished in 1933, the new <a href="/wiki/Modernism_(architecture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernism (architecture)">modernist</a> premises of the Warsaw airport cost the <a href="/wiki/State_Treasury" class="mw-redirect" title="State Treasury">State Treasury</a> around 10&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Zloty" class="mw-redirect" title="Zloty">Zloty</a>. The new complex included three hangars, exhibition space, garages, and of course a large, modern terminal building with a concrete taxiway complete with stands for a number of aircraft. Warsaw thus received an airport befitting of any European capital city. In its first year of operation, Ok\xc4\x99cie served around 10,750 passengers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> After the aerodrome\'s civilian buildings were finished, the military potential of the site began to be developed, with a <a href="/wiki/Polish_Air_Force" title="Polish Air Force">Polish Air Force</a> base opening soon after; later followed the buildings of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Aviation,_Warsaw" title="Institute of Aviation, Warsaw">Institute of Aviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/PZL" title="PZL">PZL</a> aircraft-building plant and other pieces of aviation infrastructure.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>As air traffic and the number of aircraft movements grew greatly year on year, the authorities identified the need to develop a new system for air traffic navigation and control. The state, as a result, marked a number of air corridors for use by civil airlines, whilst radio stations were established to regulate such traffic and divert it away from sensitive and restricted areas. By 1938, the airport was equipped with 16 immigration checkpoints for passengers both departing and arriving on international flights. These posts were then manned by the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Border_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Border Guard">Polish Border Guard</a>. By 1937, the airport had also received new radio navigation equipment and was using <a href="/wiki/Lorenz_beam" title="Lorenz beam">Lorenz beam</a> technology to assure the safety of landings and approaches over <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, during periods of poor visibility or bad weather. On the eve of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Ok\xc4\x99cie airport was connected by regular scheduled flights with 6 domestic and 17 foreign airports, among which were <a href="/wiki/Tel-Aviv" class="mw-redirect" title="Tel-Aviv">Tel-Aviv</a> (then in <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a> in Lebanon; there were also plans to soon begin transatlantic service to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During World War II, Ok\xc4\x99cie was often used as a battleground between the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(Wehrmacht)" class="mw-redirect" title="German Army (Wehrmacht)">German Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polish_resistance_movement_in_World_War_II" title="Polish resistance movement in World War II">Polish resistance</a> and was almost completely destroyed. From the very first day of the war in Poland, Ok\xc4\x99cie became a target for bombing by the German <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a>. Later, once Warsaw was occupied by the German army, the airport became the base for two German aviation schools and a <a href="/wiki/Junkers" title="Junkers">Junkers</a> aircraft repair works. During this period, the airport also received its first concrete runway and taxiways; these were left undamaged until the very final days of the war, despite numerous attacks by both the <a href="/wiki/Home_Army" title="Home Army">Home Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Armed_Forces" title="Soviet Armed Forces">Soviet Armed Forces</a>. However, with the German withdrawal from the city, both Ok\xc4\x99cie\'s remaining buildings and ground infrastructure (including the runway) were intentionally destroyed in order to deny their use to the advancing <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polish_First_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish First Army">Polish First Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Rebuilding_Ok.C4.99cie_in_the_years_1945.E2.80.9389"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebuilding_Ok\xc4\x99cie_in_the_years_1945\xe2\x80\x9389">Rebuilding Ok\xc4\x99cie in the years 1945\xe2\x80\x9389</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rebuilding Ok\xc4\x99cie in the years 1945\xe2\x80\x9389">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-0728,_Warschau,_zerst%C3%B6rte_Halle_der_PZL-Werke.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-0728%2C_Warschau%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Halle_der_PZL-Werke.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-0728%2C_Warschau%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Halle_der_PZL-Werke.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-0728%2C_Warschau%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Halle_der_PZL-Werke.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-0728%2C_Warschau%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Halle_der_PZL-Werke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-0728%2C_Warschau%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Halle_der_PZL-Werke.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-0728%2C_Warschau%2C_zerst%C3%B6rte_Halle_der_PZL-Werke.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_141-0728,_Warschau,_zerst%C3%B6rte_Halle_der_PZL-Werke.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The destroyed <a href="/wiki/PZL" title="PZL">PZL</a> works at Warsaw Ok\xc4\x99cie in 1939.</div></div></div>\n<p>After the war, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a> resumed operations at Ok\xc4\x99cie using what was left of the pre-war infrastructure; the airline was also responsible for initiating reconstruction efforts at the airport, and soon, within two years, a new terminal, control tower and a number of stands for aircraft based at and visiting the new Ok\xc4\x99cie had been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of the 1940s, the airport had been reconnected with most of Poland\'s most important cities and a number of international services, including those to Belgrade, Berlin, Bucharest, Budapest, Brussels, Copenhagen, Prague and Stockholm. In the first half of the 1950s, this development continued and the airport authorities continued to hold talks with many international airlines on the subject of opening routes to Warsaw. In 1956, maintenance of Ok\xc4\x99cie was transferred from <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a> to state administration, then later in 1959, on the government\'s initiative, a decision was made to reconstruct the airport\'s main terminal; this, however, did not actually take place until 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The new civil aviation authority began to exercise control over airports, air corridors and routing, ground aviation infrastructure and the responsibility for entering into and signing aviation accords with other states. This gave the authority effectively complete control over Warsaw\'s airport.\n</p><p>In 1961, the airport\'s management board decided to purchase a radar for civilian air traffic control and to begin the expansion of the airport in Warsaw. The winning design for a new terminal by Jan and Krystyna Dobrowolski referred to modern architectural solutions used in many western airports. In planning, it was ordered that the initial capacity of the new \'International Airport Station\' (Mi\xc4\x99dznarodowy Dworzec Lotniczy) should be about 1&#160;million passengers a year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1962, work began on the technical design of the new terminal, and two years later, construction started. At the same time on the opposite side of the airport, a new Air Traffic Control Centre (CKRL) was established along with the airport control tower. At this time, new radar, navigational and lighting systems for operations were also purchased. Runways 1 and 3 were also thoroughly renovated.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_Okecie_airport_old_tower_March_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Warsaw_Okecie_airport_old_tower_March_2003.jpg/220px-Warsaw_Okecie_airport_old_tower_March_2003.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Warsaw_Okecie_airport_old_tower_March_2003.jpg/330px-Warsaw_Okecie_airport_old_tower_March_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Warsaw_Okecie_airport_old_tower_March_2003.jpg/440px-Warsaw_Okecie_airport_old_tower_March_2003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1444" data-file-height="1157" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_Okecie_airport_old_tower_March_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1960s terminal buildings at Warsaw\'s Chopin airport in 2003 (since demolished)</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1969, the new terminal officially became operational, with it celebrating, just one year later, its first million passengers served. However, it soon became apparent that the new terminal was too small. As a result of this situation, and to alleviate the problems it was causing, part of the airport\'s administrative office was moved to the south of the terminal and into makeshift buildings and the old airport premises on Ul. 17 Stycznia. A new separate, temporary arrival hall was then built. Meanwhile, domestic flights continued to operate from the facilities built on the site of the pre-war terminal. Some years later, in 1979, a new arrivals hall, the so-called \'Finnish Hall\' opened. Thereafter, there was a further upgrade to the airport\'s runways, and after the renovation of runways 1 and 3, runway 2 was re-designated as taxiway \'Delta\'; this was because of its location on the same axis as a number of major obstacles, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Culture_and_Science" title="Palace of Culture and Science">Palace of Culture and Science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raszyn_radio_transmitter" title="Raszyn radio transmitter">Raszyn radio transmitter</a>.\n</p><p>Political events of the early 1980s caused a decline in passenger traffic, but already by 1983, there was renewed growth, especially on international routes. However, it turned out that the existing airport infrastructure was not able to handle as much traffic as the airport was dealing with by this period; thus, in November 1986, the Government decided to expand the airport. In the face of economic reform in the late 1980s, there was also a need to create a new managing body for airports and air traffic in Poland. In October 1987, a new company, the State Enterprise "Polish Airports" (PPL), an independent, self-governing and self-financing entity of the national economy, replaced the state aviation administration as the manager of the airport. The company was managed under the authority of the minister responsible for communications and transport was responsible.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Post-communist_development_.28since_1989.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-communist_development_(since_1989)">Post-communist development (since 1989)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post-communist development (since 1989)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Budowapirsupoludniowegi-marzec2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Budowapirsupoludniowegi-marzec2005.jpg/220px-Budowapirsupoludniowegi-marzec2005.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Budowapirsupoludniowegi-marzec2005.jpg/330px-Budowapirsupoludniowegi-marzec2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Budowapirsupoludniowegi-marzec2005.jpg/440px-Budowapirsupoludniowegi-marzec2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1593" data-file-height="995" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Budowapirsupoludniowegi-marzec2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ongoing construction of Terminal 2 at Warsaw Chopin in 2005.</div></div></div>\n<p>It was only in 1990, after the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_communism" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of communism">fall of communism</a>, that a new terminal started to be built at Ok\xc4\x99cie. The main contractor was the German company <a href="/wiki/Hochtief" title="Hochtief">Hochtief</a>, and the work involved some 164 subcontractors, of which 121 were Polish companies. After 24&#160;months, the new terminal was completed at the expense of some 300&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">German marks</a>. A network of multi-storey car parks and access roads was also built, and with their completion, Warsaw gained a modern terminal with a capacity of 3.5&#160;million passengers a year. The terminal began to operate on 1 July 1992, with the first travellers to use it being those returning from Athens, Bangkok, Dubai and New York. Ten days later, the airport celebrated the first passengers departing from the new Warsaw Ok\xc4\x99cie. In the departure hall at that time, there were 26 check-in desks; however, in subsequent years of operation, passenger traffic grew rapidly. In 1993, the airport handled nearly 2.2&#160;million passengers, while six years later, this figure climbed to 4&#160;million. Eventually, the decision was taken to increase the number of available check-in desks to 33, and then to 46, consequently increasing the terminal\'s capacity to 6&#160;million passengers a year.\n</p><p>In March 2001, Warsaw Airport was renamed in honour of the renowned Polish pianist and composer <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric Chopin">Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric Chopin</a> (though this name is almost never used by residents of Warsaw, and most frequent visitors know the airport simply as Ok\xc4\x99cie). A year later, a tender for the construction of a new passenger terminal at Warsaw airport was announced, this was then won by the Polish-Spanish consortium of <a href="/wiki/Ferrovial" title="Ferrovial">Ferrovial Agrom\xc3\xa1n</a>, Budimex and <a href="/wiki/Estudio_Lamela" title="Estudio Lamela">Estudio Lamela</a>, who joined in 2004 to implement the largest Polish investment in civil aviation history, Chopin Airport\'s long-awaited \'Terminal 2\'. By 2006, the arrivals level of this new terminal had been inaugurated, with the departures level finally, after a long delay due to certification issues, being opened in late 2007. In this same year, the low-cost Etiuda terminal was also opened; this, however, was closed again just two years later in 2009, with all operations being transferred to terminals 1 and 2. The final and most recent developments in the airport\'s history came in the period covering 2010\xe2\x80\x932011, when the airport\'s new central and south piers were finished (left unfinished until the possibility of connecting them with the north pier appeared) and opened along with a redesigned terminal complex which saw the airport\'s two terminals merged to form a single \'Terminal A\' complex. Despite this, work continues on reconstructing taxiways, ramps and access roads, the most important projects of which will see the airport connected to Poland\'s expressway network via the <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S79_(Poland)" title="Expressway S79 (Poland)">S79 Airport Expressway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S2_(Poland)" title="Expressway S2 (Poland)">S2 Southern Warsaw Bypass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> An underground railway station connected to Warsaw\'s <a href="/wiki/Szybka_Kolej_Miejska_(Warsaw)" title="Szybka Kolej Miejska (Warsaw)">suburban rail system</a> was opened in June 2012 in time for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> football championships.\n</p><p>As of July 2015, the airport is managed by the State Enterprise "Polish Airports" (PPL), which has existed since 1987 and deals with construction and operation of airports and provision of services to passengers and airlines. PPL is owned and managed by the Ministry of Infrastructure and Development, in line with the 1987 Act.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The airport has two intersecting runways, whose configuration and available taxiways under current rules permit 34 passenger operations (<a href="/wiki/Takeoff" title="Takeoff">takeoffs</a> or <a href="/wiki/Landing" title="Landing">landings</a>) per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-tur-info_polish_source_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tur-info_polish_source-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preferential_runways">Preferential runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Preferential runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following preferential runway system has been established for the airport:<sup id="cite_ref-boeing_co._datasheet_on_WAW/EPWA_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boeing_co._datasheet_on_WAW/EPWA-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table>\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top; width:40%;">\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrivals"><span class="anchor" id="Arrivals"></span>Arrivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Arrivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ol><li>Runway 33</li>\n<li>Runway 11</li>\n<li>Runway 15</li>\n<li>Runway 29</li></ol>\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top; width:40%;">\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Departures"><span class="anchor" id="Departures"></span>Departures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Departures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ol><li>Runway 29</li>\n<li>Runway 15</li>\n<li>Runway 33</li>\n<li>Runway 11</li></ol>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Between 20:00 and 04:00&#160;hours (in winter: 21:00 and 05:00), Runway 15/33 is used, weather and technical considerations permitting.<sup id="cite_ref-boeing_co._datasheet_on_WAW/EPWA_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boeing_co._datasheet_on_WAW/EPWA-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_A_Warsaw_Chopin_Airport.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Terminal_A_Warsaw_Chopin_Airport.JPG/220px-Terminal_A_Warsaw_Chopin_Airport.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Terminal_A_Warsaw_Chopin_Airport.JPG/330px-Terminal_A_Warsaw_Chopin_Airport.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Terminal_A_Warsaw_Chopin_Airport.JPG/440px-Terminal_A_Warsaw_Chopin_Airport.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4588" data-file-height="2914" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_A_Warsaw_Chopin_Airport.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Check-in hall at Terminal A</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lotnisko_Chopina_Stara_cz%C4%99%C5%9B%C4%87_Terminal_A_po_przebudowie_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Lotnisko_Chopina_Stara_cz%C4%99%C5%9B%C4%87_Terminal_A_po_przebudowie_2018.jpg/220px-Lotnisko_Chopina_Stara_cz%C4%99%C5%9B%C4%87_Terminal_A_po_przebudowie_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Lotnisko_Chopina_Stara_cz%C4%99%C5%9B%C4%87_Terminal_A_po_przebudowie_2018.jpg/440px-Lotnisko_Chopina_Stara_cz%C4%99%C5%9B%C4%87_Terminal_A_po_przebudowie_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7251" data-file-height="4667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lotnisko_Chopina_Stara_cz%C4%99%C5%9B%C4%87_Terminal_A_po_przebudowie_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Departure lounge at Terminal A</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2010, the designation of terminals had changed and the entire former Terminal 1 and Terminal 2 complex is now designated as <i>Terminal A</i> divided into five check-in areas (A, B, C, D, E) in two main halls. The complex contains 116 check-in desks. Additionally <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">Finnair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> passengers can use one of the 23 self-service check-in stands located in the Terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> There are 45 passenger gates, 27 of which are equipped with jetways.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_hall">South hall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: South hall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The south hall contains the check-in areas A and B (former <i>Terminal 1</i>) was built in 1992 with a capacity for 3.5&#160;million passengers per year to replace the ageing complex from the communist era. Initially, it handled all the traffic. Since 2007, the T2, a newly built terminal adjacent to T1, has been gradually taking over the major part of the traffic. 13 September 2012 saw the beginning of the reconstruction of the south hall. On 23 May 2015 the redesigned, reconstructed south hall was fully integrated into the \'Terminal A\' complex. Before its refurbishment, the south hall was very recognizable by Polish passengers for its very characteristically dark red colour of many construction elements, including the roof that covered the departure hall, pillars, frames of doors and windows and other. In Polish it was called "buraczkowy", which simply means in the colour of beets in English.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_hall">North hall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: North hall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>This new terminal (formerly known as <i>Terminal 2</i>), featuring the check-in areas C, D and E, became fully operational on 12 March 2008, two years after the originally planned opening date. The arrivals area was in operation from mid-2007 but problems with safety certification and disagreements between the airport and the construction firm delayed full operation. The new terminal is considerably larger<sup id="cite_ref-Warsaw_Airport_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warsaw_Airport-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> than the older Terminal 1 and has taken over departures for all <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> airlines and a few other carriers. August 2014 saw Chopin Airport as one of the first European airports offering free unlimited Internet access to all its passengers and visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter flights to and from Warsaw\xe2\x80\x93Chopin:<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Athens_International_Airport" title="Athens International Airport">Athens</a> <br /><b>Seasonal:</b> <a href="/wiki/Heraklion_International_Airport" title="Heraklion International Airport">Heraklion</a> (begins 16 May 2021),<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki_Airport" title="Thessaloniki Airport">Thessaloniki</a> (begins 20 June 2021)<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <br /><b>Seasonal charter:</b> <a href="/wiki/Kalamata_International_Airport" title="Kalamata International Airport">Kalamata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kefalonia_International_Airport" title="Kefalonia International Airport">Kefalonia</a><sup id="cite_ref-grecos.pl_19-0" class="reference"><a href="/wiki/Rhodes_International_Airport" title="Rhodes International Airport">Rhodes</a>\n</td>\n<td>72,106\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation_services">Aviation services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Aviation services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Passenger handling, aircraft handling, into-plane fueling and de-icing/anti-icing services are handled by BGS.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Warsaw Chopin Airport is located in the south-west part of Warsaw, approximately 10&#160;km (6.21&#160;mi) from the city centre. The airport is easy to access by train, local buses or taxi.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:27WE-007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/27WE-007.jpg/220px-27WE-007.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/27WE-007.jpg/330px-27WE-007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/27WE-007.jpg/440px-27WE-007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:27WE-007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two <a href="/wiki/Szybka_Kolej_Miejska_(Warsaw)" title="Szybka Kolej Miejska (Warsaw)">SKM</a> trains at <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport_railway_station" title="Warsaw Chopin Airport railway station">Warsaw Chopin Airport railway station</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>A rail link was built at a cost of 230&#160;million z\xc5\x82oty to connect the airport\'s <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport_railway_station" title="Warsaw Chopin Airport railway station">Warsaw Chopin Airport railway station</a> (built as part of Terminal A) to the Warsaw city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The station was opened on 1 June 2012, with service starting on the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Trains run every 15 minutes.\n</p><p>On 15 December 2019, a direct rail service was established with the city of <a href="/wiki/Lodz" class="mw-redirect" title="Lodz">Lodz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car">Car</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Car">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Franciszek_%C5%BBwirko" title="Franciszek \xc5\xbbwirko">\xc5\xbbwirki</a> i <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Wigura" title="Stanis\xc5\x82aw Wigura">Wigury</a>, named after the celebrated aviators who won the <a href="/wiki/Challenge_International_de_Tourisme_1932" title="Challenge International de Tourisme 1932">Challenge International de Tourisme in 1932</a>, is the main artery leading to the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-airportaccess_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airportaccess-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Warsaw city centre can be reached by the bus lines: 175 and 188 during the day and N32 at night. There is also an additional line 148 that provides access to <a href="/wiki/Ursyn%C3%B3w" title="Ursyn\xc3\xb3w">Ursyn\xc3\xb3w</a> (a southern part of Warsaw) and <a href="/wiki/Praga" title="Praga">Praga</a> (an eastern part of Warsaw). Bus 331 connects with the <a href="/wiki/Wilanowska_metro_station" title="Wilanowska metro station">Wilanowska metro station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-airportaccess_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airportaccess-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 19 December 1962, a LOT Polish Airlines <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount 804</a> <a href="/wiki/1962_LOT_Vickers_Viscount_Warsaw_crash" title="1962 LOT Vickers Viscount Warsaw crash">crashed on approach</a> after a flight from Brussels and Berlin-Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport, while attempting a go-around. All 33 passengers on board died.</li>\n<li>On 14 March 1980, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines_Flight_007" class="mw-redirect" title="LOT Polish Airlines Flight 007">LOT Polish Airlines Flight 007</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-62" title="Ilyushin Il-62">Ilyushin Il-62</a> aircraft crashed on <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Final approach (aviation)">final approach</a> from New York City\'s <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a>, when attempting a <a href="/wiki/Go-around" title="Go-around">go-around</a>. All 87 passengers and crew members on board died, including the entire amateur US boxing team, Polish pop singer <a href="/wiki/Anna_Jantar" title="Anna Jantar">Anna Jantar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_P._Merriam" title="Alan P. Merriam">Alan P. Merriam</a>.</li>\n<li>On 9 May 1987, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines_Flight_5055" title="LOT Polish Airlines Flight 5055">LOT Polish Airlines Flight 5055</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-62M" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilyushin Il-62M">Ilyushin Il-62M</a> took off for a flight to New York city\'s <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> and returned to Ok\xc4\x99cie, after an engine failure. During its approach, the aircraft crashed in a heavily wooded area, short of the runway. All 183 passengers and crew members on board died.</li>\n<li>On 14 September 1993 <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_2904" title="Lufthansa Flight 2904">Lufthansa Flight 2904</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320-200">Airbus A320-200</a> overran the runway 11. It was a flight from Frankfurt, Germany. The aircraft departed the runway and rolled 90 metres (300 feet) before it hit the embankment and an LLZ aerial. A fire started and penetrated into the passenger cabin. Two of 70 occupants died in this accident, including the training captain who died on impact and one passenger who was unable to escape because he lost consciousness as a result of the smoke in the cabin.</li>\n<li>On 31 December 1993, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a> Flight 002, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767-300ER</a> arriving from <a href="/wiki/Chicago-O%27Hare_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago-O&#39;Hare International Airport">Chicago-O\'Hare International Airport</a>, suffered substantial damage after its nose gear collapsed when touching down. There were no fatalities.</li>\n<li>On 1 November 2011, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines_Flight_16" title="LOT Polish Airlines Flight 16">LOT Polish Airlines Flight 16</a>, a Boeing 767-300ER, inbound from <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a>, safely landed at Warsaw Chopin after a mechanical failure of the landing gear prior to landing. The cockpit crew successfully performed an emergency gear-up landing at the airport with no loss of life or injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw_Chopin_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Poland" title="List of airports in Poland">List of airports in Poland</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
